            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Redox-active conjugated polymers have drawn much attention as electrodes for batteries.  Among them, branched conjugated polymers (BCPs) are supposed to have advantages over linear conjugated polymers (LCPs), because the branched structure should benefit electrolyte infiltration and ionic transport and thus would contribute to high rate capability.  However, the direct comparison of BCPs with LCPs as electrodes for batteries is rarely reported because it is difficult to synthesize an LCP and a BCP with a similar chem. environment.  Herein, we design and synthesize two aza-fused conjugated polymers as anodes for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), including an LCP and a BCP with similar constructing units.  Both of them displayed outstanding Na-storage performance at a slow rate.  Particularly, the BCP anode exhibited extraordinary rate capability, which was much higher than that of the LCP anode.  The rate performance of the BCP anode even outperformed most org. polymeric anodes for SIBs.  This work provides insight into branched conjugated polymers and inspires the mol. design of novel polymers for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqx8NGsxpPNP7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li7I7RsHIIipQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXit1aks7vP&amp;md5=14bed07b826f28e5c49ab294a60c2b64</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1073/pnas.1605318113"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mahmood, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, E.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The formation of 2D polyaniline (PANI) has attracted considerable interest due to its expected electronic and optoelectronic properties.  Although PANI was discovered over 150 y ago, obtaining an atomically well-defined 2D PANI framework has been a longstanding challenge.  Here, we describe the synthesis of 2D PANI via the direct pyrolysis of hexaaminobenzene trihydrochloride single crystals in solid state.  The 2D PANI consists of three Ph rings sharing six nitrogen atoms, and its structural unit has the empirical formula of C3N.  The topol. and electronic structures of the 2D PANI were revealed by scanning tunneling microscopy and scanning tunneling spectroscopy combined with a first-principle d. functional theory calcn.  The electronic properties of pristine 2D PANI films (undoped) showed ambipolar behaviors with a Dirac point of -37 V and an av. cond. of 0.72 S/cm.  After doping with hydrochloric acid, the cond. jumped to 1.41 × 103 S/cm, which is the highest value for doped PANI reported to date.  Although the structure of 2D PANI is analogous to graphene, it contains uniformly distributed nitrogen atoms for multifunctionality; hence, we anticipate that 2D PANI has strong potential, from wet chem. to device applications, beyond linear PANI and other 2D materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpkwQS3MOBLUbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li7I7RsHIIipQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XpvFersrg%253D&amp;md5=65ec533bc59eece8fd525912e3289406</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref47'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit47" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA02431B"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zou, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">PPN (Poly-Peri-Naphthalene) Film as a Narrow-Bandgap Organic Thermoelectric Material</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A narrow-bandgap semiconducting thin film of poly-peri-naphthalene (PPN) has been synthesized via the pyrolysis of 3,4,9,10-perylenetetracarboxylic dianhydride (PTCDA).  By tuning the pyrolysis temp., the bandgap of the PPN film can be adjusted from 0.37 to 0.26 eV.  Optimized thermoelec. performance can be achieved at the pyrolytic temp. of 600 °C, at which the power factor reached up to 0.43 μW m-1 K-2, with a Seebeck coeff. of 47 μV K-1 and an elec. cond. of 1.85 S cm-1.  IR and Raman spectra indicate that the structure of the pyrolytic film is similar to that of multilayer graphene or graphene nanoribbons with a narrow bandgap.  Since the PPN film has the advantages of a tunable bandgap, low cost, feasibility for large-area fabrication, thermal and chem. stability, and a relatively high performance without further modification, it is a promising carbon-based thermoelec. material and is worth further investigations.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq7defLi4tQ97Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li7I7RsHIIipQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXmslWqs70%253D&amp;md5=eb63ec5e794522404953248bbc187b95</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref48'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit48" data-doi="10.1039/B204251G"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ajayaghosh, A.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Donor-Acceptor Type Low Band Gap Polymers: Polysquaraines and Related Systems</span>. <i>Chem. One of the approaches towards the designing of such polymers is the use of strong donor and acceptor monomers at regular arrangements in the repeating units, which has limited success in many cases.         </div><div class="casAbstract">It is a challenge to prep. org. electrodes for sodium-ion batteries with long cycle life and high capacity.  The highly reactive radical intermediates generated during the sodiation/desodiation process could be a crit. issue because of undesired side reactions.  Here we present durable electrodes with a stabilized α-C radical intermediate.  Through the resonance effect as well as steric effects, the excessive reactivity of the unpaired electron is successfully suppressed, thus developing an electrode with stable cycling for over 2,000 cycles with 96.8% capacity retention.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The carboxylate group-based org. electrode materials are promising anodes for rechargeable sodium ion batteries (SIBs) due to the low cost, abundance, environmental benignity and high sustainability of org. materials.  Here, we compare the electrochem. performance of three carboxylate group-based org. electrode materials in SIBs, and identify that the two carboxylate groups in the para position of the benzene ring are electrochem. active centers to reversibly react with Na-ions and electrons.                         cas_cit54R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">54</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Activating Aromatic Rings as Na-Ion Storage Sites to Achieve High Capacity</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yaojun; Zhao, Xiaolin; Fang, Chun; Ye, Zhao; He, Yan-Bing; Lei, Danni; Yang, Jun; Zhang, Yan; Li, Yuyu; Liu, Qing; Huang, Ying; Zeng, Rui; Kang, Litao; Liu, Jianjun; Huang, Yun-Hui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chem</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Similar to graphite and graphene, arom. rings are ultra-stable configurations with highly delocalized sp2-hybridized electrons, which are the basic units for most org. electrode materials.  However, the arom. rings in org. electrode materials are inaccessible for Na+-ion storage.  Here, we have designed a wavy-layered 3D structure of metal-org. compd. zinc perylenetetracarboxylates (Zn-PTCA) with stretched space between adjacent perylene planes, which enables arom. rings activated as Na+-ion storage sites. We believe that the present strategy can open up an avenue for developing a big family of 3D open-framework-structured org. materials for application in high-capacity Na+-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGowC9XFAMxGZ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh4Ez9iW--qMQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit55R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">55</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Successive Storage of Cations and Anions by Ligands of π-d-Conjugated Coordination Polymers Enabling Robust Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Yuan; Zhu, Qin; Fan, Kun; Gu, Yuming; Sun, Mingxuan; Li, Zengyu; Zhang, Chenyang; Wu, Yanchao; Wang, Qian; Xu, Shuaifei; Ma, Jing; Wang, Chengliang; Hu, Wenping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">60</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">34</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The oxidn. of π-d-conjugated coordination polymers (CCPs) accompanied with anion insertion has the merits of increasing the capacity and elevating the discharge voltages.  However, previous reports on this mechanism either required more investigations or showed low capacity and poor cyclablity.  Herein, triphenylene-catecholate-based two-dimensional CCPs are constructed by employing inactive transition-metal ions (Zn2+) as nodes, forming Zn-HHTP.  Substantial characterizations and theor. calcns. indicate the successive storage of cations and anions by redox reactions of only ligands, leading to a high reversible capacity of ∼ 150 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1 and a remarkable capacity retention of 90% after 1000 cycles.  On the contrary, as a control expt., the analogous CCPs (Cu-HHTP) with Cu2+ nodes, where both ligands and metal ions undergo redox reactions, accompanied by the storage of only Na+ cations, show a much poorer cyclability.  These results highlight the importance of redox reactions of only ligands for long-term cycle life and the insight into the storage mechanisms deepens our understanding on CCPs for the further design of CCPs with high performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr335MICGqLS7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhiEv-phvFgxw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhs1emtLvI&amp;md5=9aa134081025dcc357e358daaf54b2a7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref56"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref56'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">56</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit56" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201402402"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Castillo-Martínez, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Carretero-González, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Armand, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Polymeric Schiff Bases as Low-Voltage Redox Centers for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Angew.                         cas_cit56R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">56</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Polymeric Schiff Bases as Low-Voltage Redox Centers for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Castillo-Martinez, Elizabeth; Carretero-Gonzalez, Javier; Armand, Michel</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The redox entity comprising two Schiff base groups attached to a Ph ring (of structure [-N=CH-Ar-CH=N-]) is reported to be active for sodium-ion storage (Ar = arom. group).  Electroactive polymeric Schiff bases were produced by reaction between non-conjugated aliph. or conjugated arom. diamine block with terephthalaldehyde unit.  Cryst. polymeric Schiff bases are able to electrochem. store more than one sodium atom per azomethine group at potentials between 0 and 1.5 V vs. Na+/Na.  The redox potential can be tuned through conjugation of the polymeric chain and by electron injection from donor substituents in the arom. rings.  Reversible capacities of up to 350 mA h g-1 are achieved when the carbon mixt. is optimized with Ketjen Black.  Interestingly, the "reverse" configuration (of structure [-CH=N-Ar-N=CH-]) is not electrochem. active, though isoelectronic.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrfY8JYZw4ZirVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhiEv-phvFgxw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXmslakur4%253D&amp;md5=53412644537ae0ee4c6334a00b670423</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref57"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref57'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">57</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit57" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.9b07360"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Few-Layered Fluorinated Triazine-Based Covalent Organic Nanosheets for High-Performance Alkali Organic Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Nano</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>13</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">14252</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">14261</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit57R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">57</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Few-Layered Fluorinated Triazine-Based Covalent Organic Nanosheets for High-Performance Alkali Organic Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Hang; Sun, Weiwei; Chen, Xiudong; Wang, Yong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In order to fulfill the increasing demand for renewable energy, besides the lithium-ion batteries, other alkali (Na, K)-ion batteries are extensively investigated.  However, the difficulty to find universal and environmentally benign electrodes for these alkali (Na, K)-ion batteries still severely restricts their development.  Promising characteristics, including mol. diversity, low cost, and operation safety, endow the org. electrodes more advantages for applications in alkali-ion batteries.  However, org. electrodes usually deliver a reversible capacity smaller than that of their inorg. counterparts due to sluggish ion/electron diffusion and possible dissoln. in org. electrolytes.  This work introduces fluorine atoms into the covalent triazine frameworks (CTF) to obtain two-dimensional layered fluorinated CTF (FCTF) and its exfoliated few-layered product (E-FCTF) and uses them as anodes of Li, Na, and K org. batteries.  Exfoliated E-FCTF electrode delivers high reversible capacities, as well as excellent cycle life for alkali org. batteries (1035 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1 after 300 cycles and 581 mAh g-1 at 2 A g-1 after 1000 cycles for lithium org. batteries).  In view of the exptl. probing and the theor. calcn., the Li storage mechanism for the E-FCTF can be detd. to be an intriguing multielectronic redox reaction originated from lithium storage on the benzene ring and triazine ring units.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoINuzKGOBtyrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhiEv-phvFgxw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXit1OqtrnP&amp;md5=f3f2577edd09d18127b6d379ebb5cbc6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref58"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref58'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">58</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit58" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.9b05956"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Weeraratne, K.                         cas_cit58R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">58</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Redox-Active Porous Organic Polymers as Novel Electrode Materials for Green Rechargeable Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Weeraratne, K.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The use of redox-active org. materials in rechargeable batteries has the potential to transform the field by enabling lightwt., flexible, green batteries while replacing lithium with sodium would mitigate the limited supplies and high cost of lithium.  Herein, we report the first use of highly porous azo-linked polymers (ALPs) as a new redox-active electrode material for rechargeable sodium-ion batteries.  ALPs are highly cross-linked polymers and therefore eliminate the soly. issue of org. electrodes in common electrolytes, which is prominent in small org. mols. and leads to fast capacity fading.  Moreover, the high surface area coupled with the π-conjugated microporous nature of ALPs facilitates electrolyte adsorption in the pores and assists in fast ionic transport and charge transfer rates.                         cas_cit59R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">59</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Slope-Dominated Carbon Anode with High Specific Capacity and Superior Rate Capability for High Safety Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Qi, Yuruo; Lu, Yaxiang; Ding, Feixiang; Zhang, Qiangqiang; Li, Hong; Huang, Xuejie; Chen, Liquan; Hu, Yong-Sheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The comprehensive performance of carbon anodes for Na-ion batteries (NIBs) is largely restricted by their inferior rate capability and safety issues.  Herein, a slope-dominated carbon anode is achieved at a low temp. of 800°C, which delivers a high reversible capacity of 263 mA h g-1 at 0.15C with an impressive initial Coulombic efficiency (ICE) of 80%.  When paired with the NaNi1/3Fe1/3Mn1/3O2 cathode, the reversible capacity at 6C is still 75% of that at 0.15C, and 73% of the capacity is retained after 1000 cycles at 3C.  The enhanced Na storage performance could be attributed to the unique microstructure with randomly oriented short carbon layers and the relatively higher defect concn.  Given its robustness, such a low-temp. carbonization strategy could also be applicable to other precursors and provide a new opportunity to design slope-dominated carbon anodes for high safety, low-cost NIBs with excellent ICE and superior rate capability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpAy-Y5n9CtoLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhiEv-phvFgxw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXjs1GmtL0%253D&amp;md5=c82dc2dadcdd0a9cf9582ea3d65d6ffc</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref60"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref60'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">60</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit60" data-doi="10.1055/s-0032-1317696"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mahmood, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jeon, I.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lah, M.                 10.1002/advs.202000012</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D7%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D2000012%26journal%3DAdv.%2BSci.%26author%3DH.%2BHuang%26author%3DY.%2BZhao%26author%3DY.%2BBai%26author%3DF.%2BLi%26author%3DY.%2BZhang%26author%3DY.%2BChen%26title%3DConductive%2BMetal-Organic%2BFrameworks%2Bwith%2BExtra%2BMetallic%2BSites%2Bas%2Ban%2BEfficient%2BElectrocatalyst%2Bfor%2Bthe%2BHydrogen%2BEvolution%2BReaction%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadvs.202000012&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.2c11132&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadvs.202000012&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit61R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">61</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Conductive Metal-Organic Frameworks with Extra Metallic Sites as an Efficient Electrocatalyst for the Hydrogen Evolution Reaction</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Hao; Zhao, Yue; Bai, Yimin; Li, Fumin; Zhang, Ying; Chen, Yu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Science (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2000012</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ASDCCF</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2198-3844</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The 2D conductive metal-org. frameworks (MOFs) are expected to be an ideal electrocatalyst due to their high utilization of metal atoms.  Exploring a new conjugated ligand with extra active metallic center can further boost the structural advantages of conductive MOFs.  In this work, hexaiminohexaazatrinaphthalene (HAHATN) is employed as a conjugated ligand to construct bimetallic sited conductive MOFs (M23(M13[n.8729]HAHATN)2) with an extra M-N2 moiety.  D. functional theory (DFT) calcns. demonstrate that the 2D conjugated framework renders M23(M13[n.8729]HAHATN)2 a high elec. cond. with narrow bandgap (0.19 eV) for electron transfer and a favorable in-plane porous structure (2.7 nm) for mass transfer.  Moreover, the metal atom at the extra M-N2 moiety has a higher unsatn. degree than that at M-N4 linkage, resulting in a stronger ability to donate electrons for enhancing electroactivity.  These characteristics endow the new conductive MOFs with an enhanced electroactivity for hydrogen evolution reaction (HER) electrocatalysis.  Among the series of M23(M13[n.8729]HAHATN)2 MOF, Ni3(Ni3[n.8729]HAHATN)2 nanosheets with the optimal structure exhibit a small overpotential of 115 mV at 10 mA cm-2, low Tafel slope of (45.6 mV dec-1), and promising electrocatalytic stability for HER.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqtGyjDTc01F7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj_CXFo8qv4RA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhsF2js7bF&amp;md5=45941c9c24bd53d8f327b978d90de58d</span></div></div></div></div></li></ol></div><script                         rightTab-cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Black phosphorus composites with engineered interfaces for high-rate high-capacity lithium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jin, Hongchang; Xin, Sen; Chuang, Chenghao; Li, Wangda; Wang, Haiyun; Zhu, Jian; Xie, Huanyu; Zhang, Taiming; Wan, Yangyang; Qi, Zhikai; Yan, Wensheng; Lu, Ying-Rui; Chan, Ting-Shan; Wu, Xiaojun; Goodenough, John B.; Ji, Hengxing; Duan, Xiangfeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Science (Washington, DC, United States)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">370</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6513</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">192-197</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SCIEAS</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1095-9203</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Association for the Advancement of Science</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">High-rate lithium (Li) ion batteries that can be charged in minutes and store enough energy for a 350-mi driving range are highly desired for all-elec. vehicles.  A high charging rate usually leads to sacrifices in capacity and cycling stability.  The use is reported of black phosphorus (BP) as the active anode for high-rate, high-capacity Li storage.  The formation of covalent bonds with graphitic carbon restrains edge reconstruction in layered BP particles to ensure open edges for fast Li+ entry, the coating of the covalently bonded BP-graphite particles with electrolyte-swollen polyaniline yields a stable solid-electrolyte interphase and inhibits the continuous growth of poorly conducting Li fluorides and carbonates to ensure efficient Li+ transport.  The resultant composite anode demonstrates an excellent combination of capacity, rate, and cycling endurance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr_iGAQqirQRbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lirnO3pqBJTjA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXitVCrsbjP&amp;md5=cc3f720c4c8da9258eea0b038b7f916a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1038/s41563-020-0756-y"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Q.</span></span>; Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>20</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">76</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">83</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1038/s41563-020-0756-y</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Extra storage capacity in transition metal oxide lithium-ion batteries revealed by in situ magnetometry</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Qiang; Li, Hongsen; Xia, Qingtao; Hu, Zhengqiang; Zhu, Yue; Yan, Shishen; Ge, Chen; Zhang, Qinghua; Wang, Xiaoxiong; Shang, Xiantao; Fan, Shuting; Long, Yunze; Gu, Lin; Miao, Guo-Xing; Yu, Guihua; Moodera, Jagadeesh S.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">20</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">76-83</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NMAACR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1476-1122</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Research</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), many promising electrodes that are based on transition metal oxides exhibit anomalously high storage capacities beyond their theor. values.  Although this phenomenon has been widely reported, the underlying physicochem. mechanism in such materials remains elusive and is still a matter of debate.  In this work, we use in situ magnetometry to demonstrate the existence of strong surface capacitance on metal nanoparticles, and to show that a large no. of spin-polarized electrons can be stored in the already-reduced metallic nanoparticles (that are formed during discharge at low potentials in transition metal oxide LIBs), which is consistent with a space charge mechanism.  Through quantification of the surface capacitance by the variation in magnetism, we further show that this charge capacity of the surface is the dominant source of the extra capacity in the Fe3O4/Li model system, and that it also exists in CoO, NiO, FeF2 and Fe2N systems.  The space charge mechanism revealed by in situ magnetometry can therefore be generalized to a broad range of transition metal compds. for which a large electron d. of states is accessible, and provides pivotal guidance for creating advanced energy storage systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrX_3oIxgs2wrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgV6gDLyFfteA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhs1ehsrvM&amp;md5=6175baac970ba7492189f24907aa1051</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1038/s41893-020-00664-5"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yaghoobnejad
Asl, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Manthiram, A.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Toward Sustainable Batteries</span>. <i>Nat. Sustainability</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>4</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">379</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">380</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        rightTab-cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Research Development on K-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hosaka, Tomooki; Kubota, Kei; Hameed, A. Shahul; Komaba, Shinichi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Reviews (Washington, DC, United States)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Li-ion batteries (LIBs), commercialized in 1991, have the highest energy d. among practical secondary batteries and are widely utilized in electronics, elec. vehicles, and even stationary energy storage systems.  Along with the expansion of their demand and application, concern about the resources of Li and Co is growing.  Therefore, secondary batteries composed of earth-abundant elements are desired to complement LIBs.  In recent years, K-ion batteries (KIBs) have attracted significant attention as potential alternatives to LIBs.  Previous studies have developed pos. and neg. electrode materials for KIBs and demonstrated several unique advantages of KIBs over LIBs and Na-ion batteries (NIBs).  Thus, besides being free from any scarce/toxic elements, the low std. electrode potentials of K/K+ electrodes lead to high operation voltages competitive to those obsd. in LIBs.  Moreover, K+ ions exhibit faster ionic diffusion in electrolytes due to weaker interaction with solvents and anions than that of Li+ ions; this is essential to realize high-power KIBs.  This review comprehensively covers the studies on electrochem. materials for KIBs, including electrode and electrolyte materials and a discussion on recent achievements and remaining/emerging issues.  The review also includes insights into electrode reactions and solid-state ionics and nonaq. soln. chem. as well as perspectives on the research-based development of KIBs compared to those of LIBs and NIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoJrb33gTbyWrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgV6gDLyFfteA"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">High thermal stability, nonflammability, and no liq. leakage are indispensable capabilities for electrolytes in sodium-ion batteries toward large-scale energy storage systems.  The use of solid-state or gel polymer electrolytes has proven to be one of the enabling tools to bring about these advancements; however, their application suffer from tedious synthesis procedure and/or lowionic transport to ensure a battery operation.  Herein, a novel gel polymer electrolyte with a cross-linked polyether network (GPE-CPN) was crafted through a self-catalyzed strategy, where in situ copolymn. of two monomers, 1,3-dioxolane and trimethylolpropane triglycidyl ether is realized successfully, with the use of sodium hexafluorophosphate (NaPF6) as an initiator, at room temp.  We demonstrate that the resultant GPE-CPN possesses a superior electrochem. stability window up to 4 V vs. Na+/Na, a considerable ionic cond., of 8.2 x 10-4S cm-1 at room temp., which is a capability good enough to suppress the growth of sodium dendrites and thus, stabilize the interface of electrolyte/sodium anode.  Considering the benefit from its facile fabrication and superior characteristics, the asgenerated GPE-CPN reveals a potential application for future rechargeable sodium batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpC1ObdtRef27Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgV6gDLyFfteA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhslyls7bO&amp;md5=e117964a20bb8675c2dc9fd031cf418f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref7" class="rightTabRefNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit7" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2022.140403"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Meghnani, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Singh, R.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries have gained widespread attention for energy storage devices because of low cost and high abundance of sodium sources.  In this paper, Biphasic O'3/O3 layered NaNi0.815Co0.15Al0.035O2 cathode materials (Na-NCA) are synthesized by using three different chem. routes viz. copptn., hydrothermal and sol-gel methods.  X-ray diffraction pattern and Raman anal. show the clear evidence of layered structure of all three samples.  The kinetics of sodium ion [Na+] is deduced from cyclic voltammetry techniques and the values of Na+ ion diffusion coeff. is found to be 1.62 x 10-12, 1.11 x 10-13 and 1.71 x 10-12cm2s-1 for Na-NCA synthesized by copptn., sol-gel and hydrothermal methods, resp. implying the better kinetics of Na+- ions in hydrothermal prepd. Na-NCA cathode.  Furthermore, the Cyclic voltammetry and differential capacity vs. voltage (dQ/dV vs.V) studies reveal the good reversibility of phase transition in cathode prepd. using hydrothermal route.  Electrochem. testing indicates the better performance of hydrothermally prepd. Na-NCA in terms of discharge capacity, capacity retention and energy d.  This improved electrochem. performance is attributed to decease in solid electrolyte interface, reversible phase transition and high surface area as well as better diffusion coeff.  Addnl., evolution of phase after cycling process are also investigated and only single O'3 phase is obsd. for hydrothermal prepd. Na-NCA cathode which is highly stable at room temp.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr3PlwHtL-wU7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg0qTlNEQk3Yg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XhtFWhsrfJ&amp;md5=3c8d4c21adb38ffbdf3577a1b79d8baf</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref8" class="rightTabRefNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit8" data-doi="10.1038/s41578-021-00324-w"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Usiskin, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Popovic, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Law, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Balaya, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Maier, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Fundamentals, Status and Promise of Sodium-Based Batteries</span>. <i>Nat.     <span class="NLM_cas:volume">46</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3529-3614</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CSRVBR</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Energy prodn. and storage technologies have attracted a great deal of attention for day-to-day applications.  In recent decades, advances in lithium-ion battery (LIB) technol. have improved living conditions around the globe.  LIBs are used in most mobile electronic devices as well as in zero-emission electronic vehicles.  However, there are increasing concerns regarding load leveling of renewable energy sources and the smart grid as well as the sustainability of lithium sources due to their limited availability and consequent expected price increase.  Therefore, whether LIBs alone can satisfy the rising demand for small- and/or mid-to-large-format energy storage applications remains unclear.  To mitigate these issues, recent research has focused on alternative energy storage systems.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as the best candidate power sources because sodium is widely available and exhibits similar chem. to that of LIBs; therefore, SIBs are promising next-generation alternatives.  Recently, sodiated layer transition metal oxides, phosphates and org. compds. have been introduced as cathode materials for SIBs.  Simultaneously, recent developments have been facilitated by the use of select carbonaceous materials, transition metal oxides (or sulfides), and intermetallic and org. compds. as anodes for SIBs.  Apart from electrode materials, suitable electrolytes, additives, and binders are equally important for the development of practical SIBs.  Despite developments in electrode materials and other components, there remain several challenges, including cell design and electrode balancing, in the application of sodium ion cells.  In this article, we summarize and discuss current research on materials and propose future directions for SIBs.  This will provide important insights into scientific and practical issues in the development of SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGot-2IKXj-Q-7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lizGP_f4HtzIQ"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">The morphol., size and phase of the material play a crucial role in its electrochem. performance.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Wrapping of reduced graphene oxide (RGO) over 2D layered transition metal oxide cathode material is very prevailing strategy to improve the capacity and cycling performance of cathode materials for sodium-batteries.  However, poorly dispersed RGO in aq. medium restricts the proper attachment of active-material with RGO resulting in non-uniform wrapping.  Herein, graphene oxide is functionalized non-covalently through multifunctional agent dextran and reduced moderately to dextran functionalized-RGO (Dx-RGO).  Further, it is attached chem. with Na[Ni0.60Mn0.35Co0.05]O2 (NMC) nano-sphere, which is synthesized by co-pptn. method. The surface-modified NMC-Dx-RGO cathode material exhibits high discharge capacity of 151 mAh g-1 at 0.1C and 55% capacity retention after 120 cycles at 0.2C.  Dx-RGO layer acts as conducting network around NMC providing uniform state of charge distribution (SOC), which facilitates fast transport of electrons.                         rightTab-cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Origin of low sodium capacity in graphite and generally weak substrate binding of Na and Mg among alkali and alkaline earth metals</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yuanyue; Merinov, Boris V.; Goddard, William A., III</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Proceedings of the National Academy of Sciences of the United States of America</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">National Academy of Sciences</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">It is well known that graphite has a low capacity for Na but a high capacity for other alkali metals.  The growing interest in alternative cation batteries beyond Li makes it particularly important to elucidate the origin of this behavior, which is not well understood.  In examg. this question, we find a quite general phenomenon: among the alkali and alk. earth metals, Na and Mg generally have the weakest chem. binding to a given substrate, compared with the other elements in the same column of the periodic table.  We demonstrate this with quantum mechanics calcns. for a wide range of substrate materials (not limited to C) covering a variety of structures and chem. compns.  The phenomenon arises from the competition between trends in the ionization energy and the ion-substrate coupling, down the columns of the periodic table.  Consequently, the cathodic voltage for Na and Mg is expected to be lower than those for other metals in the same column.  This generality provides a basis for analyzing the binding of alkali and alk. earth metal atoms over a broad range of systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqG9prmFwcZp7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lizGP_f4HtzIQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XksFCmurg%253D&amp;md5=2ec00a4075b09ef2fd0b5cc70012aa89</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref15" class="rightTabRefNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit15" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.1c01518"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luan, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pang, W.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Phase transition engineering, with the ability to alter the electronic structure and physicochem. properties of materials, has been widely used to achieve the thermodynamically unstable metallic phase MoS2 (1T-MoS2), although the complex operating conditions and low yield of previous strategies make the large-scale fabrication of 1T-MoS2 a big challenge.  Herein, we report a facile electron injection strategy for phase transition engineering and fabricate a composite of conductive TiO chem. bonded to 1T-MoS2 nanoflowers (TiO-1T-MoS2 NFs) on a large scale.  The underlying mechanism anal. reveals that electron-injection-engineering triggers a reorganization of the Mo 4d orbitals and results in a 100% phase transition of MoS2 from 2H to 1T.  In the TiO-1T-MoS2 NFs composite, the 1T-MoS2 demonstrates a higher electronic cond., a lower Na+ diffusion barrier, and a more restricted S release than 2H-MoS2.  In addn., conductive TiO bonding successfully resolves the stability challenge of the 1T phase.  These merits endow TiO-1T-MoS2 NFs electrodes with an excellent rate capability (650/288 mAh g-1 at 50/20 000 mA g-1, resp.) and an outstanding cyclability (501 mAh g-1 at 1000 mA g-1 after 700 cycles) in sodium ion batteries.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Because of concerns regarding shortages of lithium resources and the urgent need to develop low-cost and high-efficiency energy-storage systems, research and applications of sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have re-emerged in recent years.  Herein, recent advances in high-capacity Sn-based anode materials for stable SIBs are highlighted, including tin (Sn) alloys, Sn oxides, Sn sulfides, Sn selenides, Sn phosphides, and their composites.  The reaction mechanisms between Sn-based materials and sodium are clarified.  Multiphase and multiscale structural optimizations of Sn-based materials to achieve good sodium-storage performance are emphasized.  Full-cell designs using Sn-based materials as anodes and further development of Sn-based materials are discussed from a commercialization perspective.  Insights into the prepn. of future high-performance Sn-based anode materials and the construction of sodium-ion full batteries with a high energy d. and long service life are provided.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo9Gn39pP64ELVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhF6oQhj8bKHQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XmsFWiug%253D%253D&amp;md5=ea174905b562a0a4349fbcf3027fcf92</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref19" class="rightTabRefNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit19" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201903891"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Maitra, U.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Langsdorf, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Janek, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Schröder, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Design Strategies to Enable the Efficient Use of Sodium Metal Anodes in High-Energy Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Sodium-based batteries have attracted considerable attention and are recognized as ideal candidates for large-scale and low-cost energy storage.  Sodium (Na) metal anodes are considered as one of the most promising anodes for next-generation, high-energy, Na-based batteries owing to their high theor. specific capacity (1166 mA h g-1) and low std. electrode potential.  Herein, an overview of the recent developments in Na metal anodes for high-energy batteries is provided.  The high reactivity and large vol. expansion of Na metal anodes during charge and discharge make the electrode/electrolyte interphase unstable, leading to the formation of Na dendrites, short cycle life, and safety issues.  Design strategies to enable the efficient use of Na metal anodes are elucidated, including liq. electrolyte engineering, electrode/electrolyte interface optimization, sophisticated electrode construction, and solid electrolyte engineering.  Finally, the remaining challenges and future research directions are identified.  It is hoped that this progress report will shape a consistent view of this field and provide inspiration for future research to improve Na metal anodes and enable the development of high-energy sodium batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqzjTrnnlAmYrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhF6oQhj8bKHQ"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">Metal-org. frameworks (MOFs) are promising materials with fascinating properties.  Their widespread applications are sometimes hindered by the intrinsic instability of frameworks.  However, this instability of MOFs can also be exploited for useful purposes.  Herein, we report the use of MOFs as metal ion precursors for constructing functional nanocomposites by utilizing the instability of MOFs.  The heterogeneous growth process of nanostructures on substrates involves the release of metal ions, nucleation on substrates, and formation of a covering structure.  Specifically, the synthesized CoS with carbon nanotubes as substrates display enhanced performance in a lithium-ion battery.  Such strategy not only presents a new way for exploiting the instability of MOFs but also supplies a prospect for designing versatile functional nanocomposites.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoXoVBCJXrIW7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhF6oQhj8bKHQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXktFSktL0%253D&amp;md5=ceae12e861a017ff697bd6e94b13b22c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref21" class="rightTabRefNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit21" data-doi="10.1016/j.esci.2021.09.003"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ye, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Integration of Homogeneous and Heterogeneous Nucleation Growth via 3D Alloy Framework for Stable Na/K Metal Anode</span>. <i>eScience</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>1</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">75</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">82</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Rechargeable sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered attractive alternatives to lithium-ion batteries for next-generation sustainable and large-scale electrochem. energy storage.  Org. sodium-ion batteries (OSIBs) using environmentally benign org. materials as electrodes, which demonstrate high energy/power d. and good structural designability, have recently attracted great attention.  Nevertheless, the practical applications and popularization of OSIBs are generally restricted by the intrinsic disadvantages related to org. electrodes, such as their low cond., poor stability, and high soly. in electrolytes.  Here, the latest research progress with regard to electrode materials of OSIBs, ranging from small mols. to org. polymers, is systematically reviewed, with the main focus on the mol. structure design/modification, the electrochem. behavior, and the corresponding charge-storage mechanism.  Particularly, the challenges faced by OSIBs and the effective design strategies are comprehensively summarized from three aspects: function-oriented mol. design, micromorphol. regulation, and construction of org.-inorg. composites. Abstr.: Org. materials have attracted much attention for their utility as lithium-battery electrodes because their tunable structures can be sustainably prepd. from abundant precursors in an environmentally friendly manner.  Most research into org. electrodes has focused on the material level instead of evaluating performance in practical batteries.  This Review addresses this by first providing an overview of the history and redox of org. electrode materials and then evaluating the prospects and remaining challenges of org. electrode materials for practical lithium batteries. We posit that research in this field must focus more on the intrinsic electronic cond. and d. of org. electrode materials, after which a comprehensive optimization of full batteries should be performed under practically relevant conditions.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Radicals are inevitable intermediates during the charging and discharging of org. redox electrodes.  The increase of the reactivity of the radical intermediates is desirable to maximize the capacity and enhance the rate capability but is detrimental to cycling stability.  Therefore, it is a great challenge to controllably balance the redox reactivity and stability of radical intermediates to optimize the electrochem. properties with a good combination of high specific capacity, excellent rate capability, and long-term cycle life.  Herein, we reported the redox and tunable stability of radical intermediates in covalent org. frameworks (COFs) considered as high capacity and stable anode for sodium-ion batteries.  The comprehensive characterizations combined with theor. simulation confirmed that the redox of C-O· and α-C radical intermediates play an important role in the sodiation/desodiation process.  Specifically, the stacking behavior could be feasibly tuned by the thickness of 2D COFs, essentially detg. the redox reactivity and stability of the α-C radical intermediates and their contributive capacity.  The modulation of reversible redox chem. and stabilization mechanism of radical intermediates in COFs offers a novel entry to design novel high performance org. electrode materials for energy storage and conversion.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpPzOcqEyNgVbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg_zulAdngmHg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhtVektrnM&amp;md5=a21881c5d5f0abcf513bb0289ad60378</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref27" class="rightTabRefNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit27" data-doi="10.1038/s41467-019-13739-5"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nitrogen-Rich Covalent Organic Frameworks with Multiple Carbonyls for High-Performance Sodium Batteries</span>. <i>Nat.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A new metal-org. framework {(Me2NH2)2[Co3(μ3-O)(btb)2(py)(H2O)]·(DMF)2(H2O)2}n (Cobtbpy) was solvothermal synthesized (H3btb = 1,3,5-tri(4-carboxylphenyl)benzene, py = pyridine, DMF = N,N-dimethylformamide).                         rightTab-cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon- and Nitrogen-Based Organic Frameworks</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sakaushi, Ken; Antonietti, Markus</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Accounts of Chemical Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">48</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1591-1600</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  This account provides an overview of org., covalent, porous frameworks and solid-state materials mainly composed of the elements carbon and nitrogen.  The structures under consideration are rather diverse and cover a wide spectrum.  This account summarizes current works on the synthetic concepts leading toward those systems and cover the application side where emphasis is set on the exploration of those systems as candidates for unusual high-performance catalysis, electrocatalysis, electrochem. energy storage, and artificial photosynthesis.  These issues are motivated by the new global energy cycles and the fact that sustainable technologies should not be based on rare and expensive resources.  The strategic design is presented of functionality in cost-effective, affordable artificial materials starting from a spectrum of simple synthetic options to end up with carbon- and nitrogen-based porous frameworks.  Following the synthetic strategies, it is demonstrated how the electronic structure of polymeric frameworks can be tuned and how this can modify property profiles in a very unexpected fashion.  Covalent triazine-based frameworks (CTFs), for instance, showed both enormously high energy and high power d. in lithium and sodium battery systems.  Other C,N-based org. frameworks, such as triazine-based graphitic carbon nitride, are suggested to show promising band gaps for many (photo)electrochem. reactions.  Nitrogen-rich carbonaceous frameworks, which are developed from C,N-based org. framework strategies, are highlighted in order to address their promising electrocatalytic properties, such as in the hydrogen evolution reaction, oxygen redn. reaction (ORR), and oxygen evolution reaction (OER).  With careful design, those materials can be multifunctional catalysts, such as a bifunctional ORR/OER electrocatalyst.  Although the majority of new C,N-based materials are still not competitive with the best (usually nonsustainable candidates) for each application, the framework/N approach as such is still in its infancy and has already moved org. materials to regions where otherwise only traditional noble metals or special inorg. semiconductors are found.  As one potential way to enhance the properties of polymeric frameworks, the idea of catalysts having unique active surfaces based on Mott-Schottky heterojunctions and related concepts are addressed.  In order to integrate all of the above versatile subjects from synthesis to applications on C,N-based org. frameworks, we begin the discussion with synthetic concepts and strategies for these frameworks to distinguish these systems from typical covalent org. frameworks based on boron oxide rings.  Next the focus is on the semiconducting properties of C,N-based org. frameworks in order to show a continuous transition between CTFs and other systems, such as graphitic carbon nitrides.  At the end, applications of these materials are shown by highlighting their properties in electrochem. energy storage and photo- and electrocatalysis.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp-zm_bIJvAcbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg_zulAdngmHg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXovFKqt7c%253D&amp;md5=dc82b5d9765958b87f9d0dabf67eec26</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref32" class="rightTabRefNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit32" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201905803"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Weng, G.-M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Karpovich, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lipton, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kong, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pfefferle, L.         </div><div class="casAbstract">2D graphitic carbon nitride (g-C3N4) nanosheets are a promising neg. electrode candidate for sodium-ion batteries (NIBs) owing to its easy scalability, low cost, chem. stability, and potentially high rate capability.  However, intrinsic g-C3N4 exhibits poor electronic cond., low reversible Na-storage capacity, and insufficient cyclability.  DFT calcns. suggest that this could be due to a large Na+ ion diffusion barrier in the innate g-C3N4 nanosheet.  A facile one-pot heating of a mixt. of low-cost urea and asphalt is strategically applied to yield stacked multilayer C/g-C3N4 composites with improved Na-storage capacity (about 2 times higher than that of g-C3N4, up to 254 mAh g-1), rate capability, and cyclability.  A C/g-C3N4 sodium-ion full cell (in which sodium rhodizonate dibasic is used as the pos. electrode) demonstrates high Coulombic efficiency (ca. 99.8 %) and a negligible capacity fading over 14 000 cycles at 1 A g-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrWaLdOYgOps7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg_zulAdngmHg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhsFyjtrvI&amp;md5=d5ffd1c1c0ef34ce42758c3651604e94</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref33" class="rightTabRefNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit33" data-doi="10.1016/j.flatc.2022.100351"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Patel, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gupta, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Singh, S.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A layered composite g-C3N4@RGO of graphitic carbon nitride (g-C3N4) and reduced graphene oxide (RGO) is reported as an anode material for rechargeable sodium ion batteries (SIBs).  Initially, conducting interconnected hydrogel RGO was prepd. by hydrothermal method and was further soaked in satd. urea soln., followed by calcination to synthesize g-C3N4@RGO composites.  The coin type half cells were prepd. by using composite g-C3N4@RGO and pristine RGO as anode and their electrochem. performances were compared.  The prepd. half-cell of the composite anode delivers max. reversible specific discharge capacity of ∼ 170 mAh.g-1 and ∼ 160 mAh.g-1 at 0.1C and at 0.2C, resp.  Whereas, prepd. half-cell using RGO anode shows max. reversible discharge capacity of ∼ 146 mAh.g-1 and ∼ 133 mAh.g-1at 0.1C and 0.2C, resp.  This composite material g-C3N4@RGO shows excellent cyclability (2000 cycles) and columbic efficiency ∼ 100% with no capacity fading compared to the RGO.  The binding of g-C3N4with RGO prevents stacking of RGO sheets and provides macro and sub-micron porous structure for smooth intercalation and trapping of Na+-ions in composite g-C3N4@RGO anode during electrochem. cycling.  The design of g-C3N4@RGO composite as a neg. electrode improves the cell performance and offers effective strategy to develop low-cost and long cycle life SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpZFBQGbMBWwrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgGO9nkMu8lpg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XntVWgtbc%253D&amp;md5=ad4b7715e69bd87b7f7bda14dd79d268</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref34" class="rightTabRefNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit34" data-doi="10.1038/natrevmats.2017.30"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kessler, F.         </div><div class="casAbstract">In the past decade, research in the field of artificial photosynthesis has shifted from simple, inorg. semiconductors to more abundant, polymeric materials.  For example, polymeric carbon nitrides have emerged as promising materials for metal-free semiconductors and metal-free photocatalysts.  Polymeric carbon nitride (melon) and related carbon nitride materials are desirable alternatives to industrially used catalysts because they are easily synthesized from abundant and inexpensive starting materials.  Furthermore, these materials are chem. benign because they do not contain heavy metal ions, thereby facilitating handling and disposal.  In this Review, we discuss the building blocks of carbon nitride materials and examine how strategies in synthesis, templating and post-processing translate from the mol. level to macroscopic properties, such as optical and electronic bandgap.  Applications of carbon nitride materials in bulk heterojunctions, laser-patterned memory devices and energy storage devices indicate that photocatalytic overall water splitting on an industrial scale may be realized in the near future and reveal a new avenue of 'post-silicon electronics'.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGptK-qluSsourVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgGO9nkMu8lpg"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Energy storage and conversion have attained significant interest owing to its important applications that reduce CO2 emission through employing green energy.  Some promising technologies are included metal-air batteries, metal-S batteries, metal-ion batteries, electrochem. capacitors, etc.  Here, metal elements are involved with Li, Na, and Mg.  For these devices, electrode materials are of importance to obtain high performance.  Two-dimensional (2D) materials are a large kind of layered structured materials with promising future as energy storage materials, which include graphene, black phosporus, MXenes, covalent org. frameworks (COFs), 2-dimensional oxides, 2-dimensional chalcogenides, and others.  Great progress was achieved to go ahead for 2-dimensional materials in energy storage and conversion.  More researchers will join in this research field.     </div><div class="casAbstract">Conjugated polymeric molecules have been heralded as promising electrode materials for the next-generation energy-storage technologies owing to their chemical flexibility at the molecular level, environmental benefit, and cost advantage.  However, before any practical implementation takes place, the low capacity, poor structural stability, and sluggish ion/electron diffusion kinetics remain the obstacles that have to be overcome.  Here, we report the synthesis of a few-layered two-dimensional covalent organic framework trapped by carbon nanotubes as the anode of lithium-ion batteries.  Remarkably, upon activation, this organic electrode delivers a large reversible capacity of 1536 mAh g(-1) and can sustain 500 cycles at 100 mA g(-1).  Aided by theoretical calculations and electrochemical probing of the electrochemical behavior at different stages of cycling, the storage mechanism is revealed to be governed by 14-electron redox chemistry for a covalent organic framework monomer with one lithium ion per C=N group and six lithium ions per benzene ring.  This work may pave the way to the development of high-capacity electrodes for organic rechargeable batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcSxfdQs24J_KGHOrQ6qeX-mfW6udTcc2eaeiklx1kOn9bntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC1MvpsFekuw%253D%253D&amp;md5=c5f604808815d9de68a8456c1578d1f7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref37" class="rightTabRefNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit37" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.1c22655"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Regulated Synthesis of α-NaVOPO<sub>4</sub> with an Enhanced Conductive Network as a High-Performance Cathode for Aqueous Na-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Porous hard carbons are synthesized via carbonizing lotus stems with naturally hierarchical structures.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The normal operation of lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) at ultralow temp. (&lt;-40°C) is significant for cold-climate applications; however, their operation is plagued by the low capacity of the conventional intercalation cathodes due to their sluggish kinetics and the slow solid diffusion of Li+ in their frameworks.  Here, it is demonstrated that amorphization is an effective strategy to promote the low-temp. dynamics of cathodes by relieving the blocking effect of a dense lattice structure on ion transport under cryogenic conditions.  As a result, due to the decreased charge transport impedance and enhanced Li+ diffusion rate, the obtained covalent amorphous polymer (CAP) with an abundance of pyrazine and carbonyl active sites displays a remarkably outstanding specific capacity of 141 mAh g-1 at -80°C, which is superior to its structural analog, a covalent cryst. polymer (43.8 mAh g-1).  Furthermore, 84.7% of the initial capacity of the CAP can be retained after 500 cycles of charge and discharge at -60°C.  Mol. dynamic simulations show that the channel-rich amorphous structure is highly conducive for lithium ions to diffuse quickly in the interstitial space of org. solids.  This work provides an effective strategy regarding the amorphization of cryst. cathodes to develop low-temp.     </div><div class="casAbstract">Potassium-ion batteries are a promising alternative to lithium-ion batteries.  However, it is challenging to achieve fast charging/discharging and long cycle life with the current electrode materials because of the sluggish potassiation kinetics.  Here we report a soft carbon anode, namely highly nitrogen-doped carbon nanofibers, with superior rate capability and cyclability.  The anode delivers reversible capacities of 248 mAh g(-1) at 25 mA g(-1) and 101 mAh g(-1) at 20 A g(-1), and retains 146 mAh g(-1) at 2 A g(-1) after 4000 cycles.
